It's interesting that the faction known for their toughness is called the Copper faction, Copper is notably weaker for Tools, Weapons and Armour than Bronze and especially Steel, Copper is a softer Metal than Iron, it's easier to deform and harder to shatter, but when it does deform it stays that way until you bend it back to it's original shape, Iron in contrast is harder and thus more brittle, but turning it into Steel makes it less Brittle  High Carbon Spring Steel is arguably the best material to forge a Sword from, it has excellent edge retention and it can deform like a Copper Blade without the deformation being permanent, or rather it literally has Spring-like Properties, as the name of the material suggests Springs are in fact made of Spring Steel, so a Sword made from it has similar properties, however the name Spring Steel covers a wide Range of different Steels as seen here: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spring_steel

Okay, I'm going to have to bring this up since nobody else is. The whole dwarves-wardens situation is HORRIFYING, do you not see that? That's the EXACT story of every indigenous community in the world that has ever been colonized, people come from the outside and steal their land and their resources and when they fight back, they are framed as the bad guys. That's what my ancestors faced at the hands of British colonizers for two centuries. I'm genuinely disappointed in you, honestly. The fact that you're trying to make up so much lore for this (and taking "inspiration" from minority communities like the native Americans for the wolf chief, etc) but you don't have the minimum courtesy to at least think twice before glorifying colonization is absolutely pathetic.  And I say this as someone who rarely gets perturbed by people doing random stuff online. Sometimes things are mistakes, and that's understandable (I'm hoping that is the situation here as well, and I hope you will rectify this.) Also, I say this as someone who has generational trauma because of British colonizers. My family was directly affected by their actions and we had to flee our home country in disgrace and terror. All less than a century ago.  And before someone comes at me and goes "hurr durr this is Minecraft chill" or "grow up it's not that deep" yes, yes it IS that deep. I absolutely do not condone cancel culture and I have seen firsthand that people can change and rectify their mistakes (whether knowingly made or not) and I definitely do believe in teaching people when something they're portraying or glorifying is wrong, especially when they have such a huge platform.

I think, when the whole project is done and dusted, a good shader (maybe even a mod) that creates specific atmospheres for all the environments would give this already jaw-dropping project a gigantic boost. For example: Thick dark fog in the woodlands, no clouds in the desert, a purple haze lingering in the mushroom swamp. Also..custom islands?   I also honestly think, that if someone took the time to create a couple plug-ins or mods, combined with the USW's immersive story and amazing areas teeming with atmosphere, I see the potential for a huge roleplaying SMP. Imagine world of warcraft, but with the flexibility of Minecraft's template. Of course, it would require immense resources to maintain, with a wide array of moderators and active server-hosts, but the implications would be huge. Imagine, different races (similar to the origins mod) with all of them residing in one part of the map, clans of warriors, knights, druids with differing abilities and ranks, like the nature centred magic of the jungle-mages, or the destructive powers of the bone tribe's shamans. With independent cultures, with their own goals and histories, the possibilities could be truly endless. You could also apply certain anti-griefing measures, like not allowing certain items to be used unless the player wielding them has a specific role (like a dwarven weaponsmith being allowed to use lava).   Just imagine: You get the greenlight to join the server, and you get directed to a selection menu, where you can pick your race and profession, with all the pros and cons of your selected class, as well as which culture you will join. You pick your role as a dwarven weaponsmith, and you are spawned into the great underground city, with the starting level of 1. You get a humble little shed, and you begin working. Your higherups give you assignments, and you carry them out. First, you are tasked with transporting metals from the mines to the great furnaces and sorting the smelted ores into their respective storage facilities. As you are promoted to level 2, you are overseeing the crafting and smelting processes, making sure the coal never runs out, and that the iron is turned into pickaxes instead of hoes. You progress higher and higher, and as you reach the higher ranks, you are introduced to the application of special kinds of enchantments, or dwarven blessings, that give dwarven armour their characteristic capabilities that distinguish them as the highest forms of craftmanship. But you may feel that this life underground doesn't really suite you as well as it once did, do you spread your wings. You venture out to the surface and seek out the greatest order of knights in the realm, and offer your special service, in exchange for high pay and a knighthood. As you can access special enchantments in the enchanting table due to your high status as a dwarven weaponsmith (this is achievable by pretty non-intrusive, complementary mods), your skills would greatly benefit the order, so they take you on, and you provide them with special enchantments for their weapons, while you get the prestigious life of a knight. Now imagine, that there are hundreds of players like you, who are all trying to make their way up the ranks in their respective fields, and you begin to see the level of fun this map could provide.  This is merely a conservative view on what an amazing experience it would be to participate in such a grand world. If we wanted to take it a little further, we could even introduce new types of weapons, armour, or food, but these are of course just speculations. The point is, if this concept were to actually manifest itself, this world would provide the basis for one of the most ground-breaking, and entertaining servers in Minecraft history. With the light sources they have or should have access to; Lava, Glow Lichen, Glow Squids, Glowstone, Shroomlight, and Soul Lanterns/Campfires, it would be enough to probably grow mushrooms.  The Glowberries are natural to the caves, the Mushrooms were traded via the Jungle Kingdom and the Cows from the Mesa. The mushrooms took easily down in the caves and became a ready supply of food both for the Dwarves and Cows, which slowly became Mooshrooms over time. They could then either be milked for Mushroom Stew or slaughtered for Beef. Other foods were more of a luxury, since they didn't keep well in the damp underground.

Games like Dragon City intentionally rig loot crates and other items in order to find a balance between keeping loot decent, but not perfect, so they buy more crates. In other words, this sort of game leeches their pay-to-win profits by convincing young adults and children to spend money they don't have. That brings me to my next point: Children. A game esentially based off the exchange of real-world currency for gambling enables kids to start (and get hooked) to gambling from a very young age. I personally do not support the idea of accepting sponsorships from selfish companies, but suit yourself.  Reguardless, before people reply to me saying, "hE hAs To MaKE monEY soMEhOW," I understand that. However, for such a large project, I can guarentee there is a large ammount of sponsorships. Even then, creators tend not to actually directly communicate to their sponsors, instead connecting through 3rd party companies, desperate to get in sponsorships for decent cuts. What I am trying to bring in to words here is that for large projects like this, pulling in millions of views, I *am certain* there are more sponsorships out here. Companies such as Social Point and Plarium Games only get in sponsorships due to their will to offer obsurd ammounts to creators, so I don't blame you for going with them.
